<p>The <b>University of Kentucky</b> (<b>UK</b>) is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_university_(U.S.)" title="State university (U.S.)">public</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Co-educational" title="Co-educational">co-educational</a> <a href="/wiki/University" title="University">university</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lexington,_Kentucky" title="Lexington, Kentucky">Lexington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">Kentucky</a>. Founded in 1865 by <a href="/wiki/John_Bryan_Bowman" title="John Bryan Bowman">John Bryan Bowman</a> as the <b>Agricultural and Mechanical College of Kentucky</b>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_HIS1_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-UK_HIS1-7">[7]</a></sup> the university is one of the state's two <a href="/wiki/Land-grant_university" title="Land-grant university">land-grant universities</a> (the other being <a href="/wiki/Kentucky_State_University" title="Kentucky State University">Kentucky State University</a>), the largest college or university in the state, with 30,720<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-booklet_2-4"><a href="#cite_note-booklet-2">[2]</a></sup> students as of Fall 2015, and the highest ranked research university in the state according to <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._News_and_World_Report" title="U.S. News and World Report">U.S. News and World Report</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FACTBOOK_0607_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-FACTBOOK_0607-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USRankings_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-USRankings-8">[8]</a></sup>
</p><p>The institution comprises 16 colleges, a <a href="/wiki/Graduate_school" title="Graduate school">graduate school</a>, 93 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Undergraduate" title="Undergraduate">undergraduate</a> programs, 99 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Master%27s_degrees" title="Master's degrees">master programs</a>, 66 <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Philosophy" title="Doctor of Philosophy">doctoral</a> programs, and four professional programs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKS_06_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-UKS_06-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="Stale cite may be suppressing current actual numbers. (February 2017)">needs update</span></a></i>]</sup> The University of Kentucky has fifteen libraries on campus. The largest is the <a href="/wiki/William_T._Young_Library" title="William T. Young Library">William T. Young Library</a>, a federal depository, hosting subjects related to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_sciences" title="Social sciences">social sciences</a>, <a href="/wiki/Humanities" title="Humanities">humanities</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Life_sciences" title="Life sciences">life sciences</a> collections. In recent years, the university has focused expenditures increasingly on research, following a compact formed by the <a href="/wiki/Kentucky_General_Assembly" title="Kentucky General Assembly">Kentucky General Assembly</a> in 1997. The directive mandated that the university become a <i>Top 20</i> public research institution, in terms of an overall ranking, to be determined by the university itself, by the year 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TOP20_why_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-TOP20_why-10">[10]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Kentucky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="University_origins">University origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Kentucky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: University origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the early commonwealth of Kentucky, higher education was limited to a number of children from prominent families, disciplined apprentices, and those young men seeking entry into clerical, legal, and medical professions. As the first university in the territory that would become Kentucky, <a href="/wiki/Transylvania_University" title="Transylvania University">Transylvania University</a> was the primary center for education, and became the father of what would become the University of Kentucky.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Barker_Hall.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="284" data-file-width="600" height="104" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Barker_Hall.jpg/220px-Barker_Hall.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Barker_Hall.jpg/330px-Barker_Hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Barker_Hall.jpg/440px-Barker_Hall.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Barker_Hall.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The early campus: Barker Hall in the center, the Main Building to the right, and a lake in the foreground where the Student Center was later built.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/John_Bryan_Bowman" title="John Bryan Bowman">John Bryan Bowman</a> founded the Agricultural and Mechanical College of Kentucky (A&amp;M), a publicly chartered department of Kentucky University, after receiving federal support through the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Morrill_Land-Grant_Colleges_Act" title="Morrill Land-Grant Colleges Act">Morrill Land-Grant Colleges Act</a> in 1865.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_HIS1_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-UK_HIS1-7">[7]</a></sup> Courses were offered at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ashland,_The_Henry_Clay_Estate" title="Ashland, The Henry Clay Estate">Ashland, The Henry Clay Estate</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKChron_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-UKChron-11">[11]</a></sup> Three years later, <a href="/wiki/James_Kennedy_Patterson" title="James Kennedy Patterson">James Kennedy Patterson</a> became the first president of the land-grant university and the first degree was awarded. In 1876, the university began to offer <a href="/wiki/Master%27s_degree" title="Master's degree">master's degree</a> programs. Two years later, A&amp;M separated from Kentucky University, which is now <a href="/wiki/Transylvania_University" title="Transylvania University">Transylvania University</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKChron_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-UKChron-11">[11]</a></sup> For the new school, Lexington donated a 52-acre (210,000 m<sup>2</sup>) park and fair ground, which became the core of UK's present campus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKChron_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-UKChron-11">[11]</a></sup> A&amp;M was initially a male-only institution, but began to admit women in 1880.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_HIS1_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-UK_HIS1-7">[7]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1892, the official colors of the university, royal blue and white, were adopted. An earlier color set, blue and light yellow, was adopted earlier at a Kentucky-<a href="/wiki/Centre_College" title="Centre College">Centre College</a> football game on December 19, 1891.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_TRAD_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-UK_TRAD-5">[5]</a></sup> The particular hue of blue was determined from a necktie, which was used to demonstrate the color of royal blue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_TRAD_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-UK_TRAD-5">[5]</a></sup>
</p><p>On February 15, 1882, <a href="/wiki/Main_Building_(University_of_Kentucky)" title="Main Building (University of Kentucky)">Administration Building</a> was the first building of three completed on the present campus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKChron_11-3"><a href="#cite_note-UKChron-11">[11]</a></sup> Three years later, the college formed the Agricultural Experiment Station, which researches issues relating to agribusiness, food processing, nutrition, water and soil resources and the environment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AES_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-AES-12">[12]</a></sup> This was followed up by the creation of the university's <i>Agricultural Extension Service</i> in 1910, which was one of the first in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_HIS2_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-UK_HIS2-13">[13]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cooperative_extension_service" title="Cooperative extension service">extension service</a> became a model of the federally mandated programs that were required beginning in 1914.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_HIS1_7-3"><a href="#cite_note-UK_HIS1-7">[7]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Coeducational_school:_Modern_period">Coeducational school: Modern period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Kentucky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Coeducational school: Modern period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Patterson_Hall_1905.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1091" data-file-width="1802" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Patterson_Hall_1905.jpg/220px-Patterson_Hall_1905.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Patterson_Hall_1905.jpg/330px-Patterson_Hall_1905.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Patterson_Hall_1905.jpg/440px-Patterson_Hall_1905.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Patterson_Hall_1905.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Patterson Hall, shortly after its 1904 opening</div></div></div>
<p>Patterson Hall, the school's first women's dormitory, was constructed in 1904. Residents had to cross a <a href="/wiki/Swamp" title="Swamp">swampy</a> depression, where the now demolished Student Center later stood, to reach central campus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_HIS1_7-4"><a href="#cite_note-UK_HIS1-7">[7]</a></sup> Four years later, the school's name was changed to the "State University, Lexington, Kentucky" upon reaching <a href="/wiki/University" title="University">university</a> status, and then to the "University of Kentucky" in 1916.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_HIS1_7-5"><a href="#cite_note-UK_HIS1-7">[7]</a></sup> The university led to the creation of the College of Home Economics in 1916, and <a href="/wiki/Mary_E._Sweeney" title="Mary E. Sweeney">Mary E. Sweeney</a> was promoted from chair of the Department of Home Economics to Dean of the College. (Later renamed the College of Human Environmental Sciences, this educational unit was folded into the College of Agriculture in 2003 as the School of Human Environmental Sciences<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup>). The College of Commerce was established in 1925, known today as the <a href="/wiki/Gatton_College_of_Business_and_Economics" title="Gatton College of Business and Economics">Gatton College of Business and Economics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_HIS2_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-UK_HIS2-13">[13]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1929, <a href="/wiki/Memorial_Hall_(University_of_Kentucky)" title="Memorial Hall (University of Kentucky)">Memorial Hall</a> was completed, dedicated to the 2,756 Kentuckians who died in <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKChron_11-4"><a href="#cite_note-UKChron-11">[11]</a></sup> This was followed up by the new <a href="/wiki/Margaret_I._King_Library" title="Margaret I. King Library">King Library</a>, which opened in 1931 and was named for a long-time library director, Margaret I. King.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKChron_11-5"><a href="#cite_note-UKChron-11">[11]</a></sup> The university's graduate and professional programs became racially integrated in 1949 when <a href="/wiki/Lyman_T._Johnson" title="Lyman T. Johnson">Lyman T. Johnson</a>, an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American" title="African American">African American</a>, won a lawsuit to be admitted to the graduate program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> African Americans would not be allowed to attend as undergraduates until 1954, following the US Supreme Court's <a href="/wiki/Brown_v._Board_of_Education" title="Brown v. Board of Education">Brown v. Board of Education</a> decision.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1939, Governor Happy Chandler appointed the first woman trustee on the University of Kentucky Board of Trustees, Georgia M. Blazer of Ashland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> She served from 1939 to 1960. In 1962, Blazer Hall was opened as the Georgia M Blazer Hall [dormitory] for Women in tribute to her twenty-one years of service as a University of Kentucky trustee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup>
</p><p>Ground was broken for the Albert B. Chandler Hospital in 1955, when Governor of Kentucky <a href="/wiki/Happy_Chandler" title="Happy Chandler">Happy Chandler</a> recommended that the Kentucky General Assembly appropriate $5 million for the creation of the University of Kentucky College of Medicine and a medical center at the university.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GB_053007_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-GB_053007-21">[21]</a></sup> This was completed after a series of studies were conducted that highlighted the health needs of the citizens, as well as the need to train more physicians for the state. Five years later, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Kentucky_College_of_Medicine" title="University of Kentucky College of Medicine">College of Medicine</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Kentucky_College_of_Nursing" title="University of Kentucky College of Nursing">College of Nursing</a> opened, followed by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Kentucky_College_of_Dentistry" title="University of Kentucky College of Dentistry">College of Dentistry</a> in 1962.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_HIS2_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-UK_HIS2-13">[13]</a></sup>
</p><p>Nine years after the founding of The Northern Extension Center in Covington, representing the Ashland Independent School Board of Education,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Ashland attorney Henderson Dysard and <a href="/wiki/Ashland_Inc." title="Ashland Inc.">Ashland Oil &amp; Refining Company</a> founder and CEO <a href="/wiki/Paul_G._Blazer" title="Paul G. Blazer">Paul G. Blazer</a> presented a proposal to President Dickey and the University of Kentucky Board of Trustees for the university to take over the day-to-day operations and curriculum of the Ashland [municipal] Junior College, creating the Ashland Center of the University of Kentucky in 1957.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> University of Kentucky Extension Centers in Fort Knox (1958), Cumberland (1960), and Henderson (1960) followed.
</p><p>In 1959, the <a href="/wiki/Patterson_School_of_Diplomacy_and_International_Commerce" title="Patterson School of Diplomacy and International Commerce">Patterson School of Diplomacy and International Commerce</a> opened and began training professionals at the master's and doctoral level for careers in international affairs. The program was the vision of UK's first president <a href="/wiki/James_Kennedy_Patterson" title="James Kennedy Patterson">James Kennedy Patterson</a> who had identified the need for the United States to develop a cadre of professionals to advance its diplomatic and commercial interests around the globe. Patterson bequeathed his entire estate to establish this entity.
</p><p>Authorized by the <a href="/wiki/Kentucky_General_Assembly" title="Kentucky General Assembly">Kentucky General Assembly</a> and signed by Governor <a href="/wiki/Bert_Combs" title="Bert Combs">Bert Combs</a> on March 6, 1962, a mandate was placed upon the University of Kentucky to form a community college system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKChron_11-6"><a href="#cite_note-UKChron-11">[11]</a></sup> Two years later, the Board of Trustees implements the legislation and established the Community College System, creating centers in <a href="/wiki/Gateway_Community_and_Technical_College" title="Gateway Community and Technical College">Covington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ashland_Community_and_Technical_College" title="Ashland Community and Technical College">Ashland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fort_Knox" title="Fort Knox">Fort Knox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Kentucky_Community_and_Technical_College" title="Southeast Kentucky Community and Technical College">Cumberland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henderson_Community_College" title="Henderson Community College">Henderson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elizabethtown_Community_and_Technical_College" title="Elizabethtown Community and Technical College">Elizabethtown</a>. In 1969, the Patterson Office Tower was completed, currently the tallest building on campus.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UKMillerHall.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="426" data-file-width="552" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/UKMillerHall.jpg/220px-UKMillerHall.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/UKMillerHall.jpg/330px-UKMillerHall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/UKMillerHall.jpg/440px-UKMillerHall.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UKMillerHall.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Miller Hall</div></div></div><p> In May 1970, students at the university began protesting the <a href="/wiki/Kent_State_shootings" title="Kent State shootings">shootings at Kent State University</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKChron_11-7"><a href="#cite_note-UKChron-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nunncenter.org_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nunncenter.org-24">[24]</a></sup> In response, Governor <a href="/wiki/Louie_Nunn" title="Louie Nunn">Louie Nunn</a> deferred to the <a href="/wiki/National_Guard_of_the_United_States" title="National Guard of the United States">National Guard</a> in an attempt to disperse the protesters. An outdated <a href="/wiki/Reserve_Officers%27_Training_Corps" title="Reserve Officers' Training Corps">ROTC</a> building was destroyed by fire. The <a href="/wiki/Louie_B._Nunn_Center_for_Oral_History" title="Louie B. Nunn Center for Oral History">Louie B. Nunn Center for Oral History</a> at the University of Kentucky Libraries has 13 oral history interviews with participants in the protests, university officials as well as former governor Nunn.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nunncenter.org_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-Nunncenter.org-24">[24]</a></sup> Nine years later, the Singletary Center for the Arts opened, named in honor of former university president Otis Singletary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKChron_11-8"><a href="#cite_note-UKChron-11">[11]</a></sup> In 1979, the University of Kentucky hosted the first Kentucky <a href="/wiki/Women_Writers_Conference" title="Women Writers Conference">Women Writers Conference</a>, which is now the longest-running conference of its kind. The Kentucky Women Writers Conference is now in its 31st year.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (July 2014)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary_history">Contemporary history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Kentucky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Contemporary history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Engineering_plaza.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2184" data-file-width="2912" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Engineering_plaza.jpg/200px-Engineering_plaza.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Engineering_plaza.jpg/300px-Engineering_plaza.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Engineering_plaza.jpg/400px-Engineering_plaza.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Engineering_plaza.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The engineering plaza.</div></div></div>
<p>In 1997, the <a href="/wiki/Kentucky_General_Assembly" title="Kentucky General Assembly">Kentucky General Assembly</a> reorganized the community college system, withdrawing the university's jurisdiction from all but the Lexington Community College.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKChron_11-9"><a href="#cite_note-UKChron-11">[11]</a></sup> The other colleges were merged with the <a href="/wiki/Kentucky_Community_and_Technical_College_System" title="Kentucky Community and Technical College System">Kentucky Technical College system</a> and were placed under a separate board of control.
</p><p>On April 3, 1998, work began on the <a href="/wiki/William_T._Young_Library" title="William T. Young Library">William T. Young Library</a>, which was the largest university project at the time of completion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HL_032298_d_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-HL_032298_d-25">[25]</a></sup> The six-level William T. Young Library was constructed on south campus and the largest book endowment among all public university libraries in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_FACTS_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-UK_FACTS-26">[26]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/William_T._Young" title="William T. Young">William T. Young</a> got his fortune from selling his peanut butter company to <a href="/wiki/Procter_%26_Gamble" title="Procter &amp; Gamble">Procter &amp; Gamble</a> in 1955. Nine years after the completion of the William T. Young Library, on April 13, 2007, an entire city block of neighborhood homes were demolished and ground was broken for the <a href="/wiki/Biological_Pharmaceutical_Complex_Building_(University_of_Kentucky)" title="Biological Pharmaceutical Complex Building (University of Kentucky)">Biological Pharmaceutical Complex Building</a>, the largest academic building in the state of Kentucky, and one of the largest in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FutureofPharmacy_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-FutureofPharmacy-27">[27]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chemistry-Physics_Building_(U.K.).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2064" data-file-width="2752" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Chemistry-Physics_Building_%28U.K.%29.jpg/200px-Chemistry-Physics_Building_%28U.K.%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Chemistry-Physics_Building_%28U.K.%29.jpg/300px-Chemistry-Physics_Building_%28U.K.%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Chemistry-Physics_Building_%28U.K.%29.jpg/400px-Chemistry-Physics_Building_%28U.K.%29.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chemistry-Physics_Building_(U.K.).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Chemistry-Physics Building</div></div></div>
<p>The Biological Pharmaceutical Complex Building complements the adjacent <a href="/wiki/Biomedical_Biological_Science_Research_Building_(University_of_Kentucky)" title="Biomedical Biological Science Research Building (University of Kentucky)">Biomedical Biological Science Research Building</a>, and is expected to be part of the new university research campus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Other recent announcements include the construction of the new $450 million <a href="/wiki/Albert_B._Chandler_Hospital" title="Albert B. Chandler Hospital">Albert B. Chandler Hospital</a>, which will was one of the largest projects in the state's history in terms of size and economic impact.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GB_053007_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-GB_053007-21">[21]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1997, the <a href="/wiki/Kentucky_General_Assembly" title="Kentucky General Assembly">Kentucky General Assembly</a> formed a compact with the university. The Top 20 Plan mandates that the University of Kentucky becomes a Top 20 public research university by 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TOP20_why_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-TOP20_why-10">[10]</a></sup> According to the compact, states with "Top 20" universities feature higher average household incomes, higher education attainments, healthier lives and more financial security.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TOP20_Presentation_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-TOP20_Presentation-29">[29]</a></sup> As a result, fewer citizens live in poverty and as a result, fewer public dollars are spent on health care.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TOP20_why_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-TOP20_why-10">[10]</a></sup> The plan would also spur technological advancements due to university-based research and increase the marketability of the state to investors.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Main_Bldg_(UK).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="405" data-file-width="600" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Main_Bldg_%28UK%29.jpg/220px-Main_Bldg_%28UK%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Main_Bldg_%28UK%29.jpg/330px-Main_Bldg_%28UK%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Main_Bldg_%28UK%29.jpg/440px-Main_Bldg_%28UK%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Main_Bldg_(UK).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Main_Building_(University_of_Kentucky)" title="Main Building (University of Kentucky)">Main Building</a> in the foreground and the Patterson Office Tower in the background</div></div></div>
<p>As part of the "Top 20" plan, the university stated that it plans to,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TOP20_why_10-3"><a href="#cite_note-TOP20_why-10">[10]</a></sup>
</p>
<ol><li>Increase enrollment by 7,000 students to 34,000;</li>
<li>Increase the state's highest graduation rate by 12% to 72%;</li>
<li>Increase the number of faculty by 625 to total 2,500;</li>
<li>Increase research expenditures by $470 million to total $768 million per year; and</li>
<li>Increase the university's role in Kentucky's "schools, farms, businesses and communities."</li></ol>
<p>The "Top 20" plan has produced some results,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TOP20_Presentation_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-TOP20_Presentation-29">[29]</a></sup>
</p>
<ol><li>Total enrollment increased from 24,061 in 1996 to 26,440 in 2004, an increase of 2,379.</li>
<li>The six-year graduation rate increased from 59.5 percent in 1998 to 61.2 percent in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></li>
<li>Research expenditures increased from $124.8 million in 1996 to $297.6 million in 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TOP20_Presentation_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-TOP20_Presentation-29">[29]</a></sup> It dipped slightly to $274 million for 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_FACTS_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-UK_FACTS-26">[26]</a></sup> It is currently ranked 28th among public universities in sponsored research.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_FACTS_26-2"><a href="#cite_note-UK_FACTS-26">[26]</a></sup></li>
<li>Endowment increased from $195.1 million in 1997 to $538.4 million in 2005.</li></ol>
<p>In 2000, to help finance the "Top 20" plan, the university launched "The Campaign for the University of Kentucky", a $600 million <a href="/wiki/Fundraising" title="Fundraising">fundraising</a> effort that was used to "enhance facilities, academic programs, public service, and scholarships."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_FACTS_26-3"><a href="#cite_note-UK_FACTS-26">[26]</a></sup> It passed that goal and the effort was raised to $1 billion. In March 2007, $1.022 billion was raised, months before the fundraising effort was set to end.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the <i>Statewide Facilities Condition Assessment Report</i> released on April 4, 2007, the university needs $12.5 billion to complete the 1997 mandate to become a "Top 20" institution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup>
</p><p>The University of Kentucky currently has an endowment of $831.8 million, as of 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HL_BillionDollar_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-HL_BillionDollar-33">[33]</a></sup> Prior endowments were $538.4 million in 2005 and $195.1 million in 1997, the rapid increases partially attributed to the "Top 20" Plan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TOP20_Presentation_29-3"><a href="#cite_note-TOP20_Presentation-29">[29]</a></sup> Currently, the William T. Young Library book endowment is the largest among public universities in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_FACTS_26-4"><a href="#cite_note-UK_FACTS-26">[26]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Kentucky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Departments">Departments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Kentucky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Departments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p>Students are divided into 16 colleges, a <a href="/wiki/Graduate_school" title="Graduate school">graduate school</a>, 93 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Undergraduate" title="Undergraduate">undergraduate</a> programs, 99 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Master%27s_degrees" title="Master's degrees">master programs</a>, 66 <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Philosophy" title="Doctor of Philosophy">doctoral</a> programs, and four professional programs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKS_06_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-UKS_06-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="Stale cite may be suppressing current actual numbers. (February 2017)">needs update</span></a></i>]</sup> The University of Kentucky has fifteen libraries on campus. The largest is William T. Young Library, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federal_depository_library" title="Federal depository library">federal depository</a>, hosting subjects related to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_sciences" title="Social sciences">social sciences</a>, <a href="/wiki/Humanities" title="Humanities">humanities</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Life_sciences" title="Life sciences">life sciences</a> collections. In recent years, the university has focused expenditures increasingly on research, following a compact formed by the <a href="/wiki/Kentucky_General_Assembly" title="Kentucky General Assembly">Kentucky General Assembly</a> in 1997. The directive mandated that the university become a <i>Top 20</i> public research institution, in terms of an overall ranking to be determined by the university itself, by the year 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TOP20_why_10-4"><a href="#cite_note-TOP20_why-10">[10]</a></sup> The university is #147 in National Universities and #75 in Top <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">Public Schools</a> in the 2019 <i>US News &amp; World Report</i> rankings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup>
</p><p>Students are divided into several colleges based on their interests and specializations:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Kentucky_College_of_Agriculture,_Food,_and_Environment" title="University of Kentucky College of Agriculture, Food, and Environment">College of Agriculture, Food and Environment</a>, founded 1908</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Kentucky_College_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="University of Kentucky College of Arts and Sciences">College of Arts and Sciences</a>, founded 1908</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gatton_College_of_Business_and_Economics" title="Gatton College of Business and Economics">Gatton College of Business and Economics</a>, founded 1925 (originally as the College of Commerce)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Kentucky_College_of_Communication_%26_Information" title="University of Kentucky College of Communication &amp; Information">College of Communication &amp; Information</a>, founded 1976</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Kentucky_College_of_Dentistry" title="University of Kentucky College of Dentistry">College of Dentistry</a>, founded 1962</li></ul>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Biological-Pharmaceutical_Building_U.K.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2184" data-file-width="2912" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Biological-Pharmaceutical_Building_U.K.jpg/250px-Biological-Pharmaceutical_Building_U.K.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Biological-Pharmaceutical_Building_U.K.jpg/375px-Biological-Pharmaceutical_Building_U.K.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Biological-Pharmaceutical_Building_U.K.jpg/500px-Biological-Pharmaceutical_Building_U.K.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Biological-Pharmaceutical_Building_U.K.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Biological_Pharmaceutical_Complex_Building_(University_of_Kentucky)" title="Biological Pharmaceutical Complex Building (University of Kentucky)">Biological-Pharmaceutical Building</a> is home to the College of Pharmacy</div></div></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Kentucky_College_of_Design" title="University of Kentucky College of Design">College of Design</a>, founded 1964 (originally the College of Architecture)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Kentucky_College_of_Education" title="University of Kentucky College of Education">College of Education</a>, founded 1923</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Kentucky_College_of_Engineering" title="University of Kentucky College of Engineering">College of Engineering</a>, founded 1918 (through a merger of the original Colleges of Civil Engineering, Mechanical Engineering, and Mines and Metals)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Kentucky_College_of_Fine_Arts" title="University of Kentucky College of Fine Arts">College of Fine Arts</a>, founded 1976</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Kentucky_College_of_Health_Sciences" title="University of Kentucky College of Health Sciences">College of Health Sciences</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> founded 1966 (originally as the College of Allied Health Personnel)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Kentucky_College_of_Law" title="University of Kentucky College of Law">College of Law</a>, founded 1908</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Kentucky_College_of_Medicine" title="University of Kentucky College of Medicine">College of Medicine</a>, founded 1954</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Kentucky_College_of_Nursing" title="University of Kentucky College of Nursing">College of Nursing</a>, founded 1956</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Kentucky_College_of_Pharmacy" title="University of Kentucky College of Pharmacy">College of Pharmacy</a>, founded 1947 (originally established in 1870 in Louisville)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Kentucky_College_of_Public_Health" title="University of Kentucky College of Public Health">College of Public Health</a>, founded 2004</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Kentucky_College_of_Social_Work" title="University of Kentucky College of Social Work">College of Social Work</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> founded 1968</li>
<li>The Graduate School,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> founded 1912</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Martin_School" title="Martin School">Martin School of Public Policy and Administration</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Patterson_School_of_Diplomacy_and_International_Commerce" title="Patterson School of Diplomacy and International Commerce">Patterson School of Diplomacy and International Commerce</a></li></ul>
<p>Other colleges no longer in existence at the University of Kentucky include the College of Library Science (separating out of the College of Arts &amp; Sciences in 1968 and incorporated in 2003 into what is now the College of Communication and Information) and the College of Home Economics (created in 1916 and whose founding dean was <a href="/wiki/Mary_E._Sweeney" title="Mary E. Sweeney">Mary E. Sweeney</a>) now a School of Human Environmental Sciences located within the College of Agriculture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Honors_program">Honors program</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Kentucky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Honors program">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Honors Program at the University of Kentucky began in 1961. It offers interdisciplinary, seminar-style classes of 15–20 students each as well as "H-section" classes that accelerate common course offerings such as chemistry, biology, and physics. The program is intended to supplement the individual interests of the students. Students are offered priority registration, one-on-one faculty attention, dedicated advising, the opportunity to engage in undergraduate research from their first semesters on campus, and are directed to other programs, including the Chellgren Fellows program, the Gaines Fellowship in the Humanities, the University Scholars Program (which allows simultaneous undergraduate and graduate study), and external scholarship opportunities. Additionally, students are offered assistance with fellowship applications, scholarship applications, study abroad opportunities, Honors designation on transcript and diploma,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> and/or service learning interests, among other things.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup>
</p><p>Beginning in 2017, the Honors Program will become the Lewis Honors College. It will be housed in the new Lewis Hall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="SECU:_SEC_Academic_Initiative">SECU: SEC Academic Initiative</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Kentucky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: SECU: SEC Academic Initiative">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The University of Kentucky is a member of the SEC Academic Consortium. Now renamed the <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Conference#The_formation_of_SECU_and_SEC_academic_network" title="Southeastern Conference">SECU</a>, the initiative was a collaborative endeavor designed to promote research, scholarship and achievement among the member universities in the <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Conference" title="Southeastern Conference">Southeastern Conference</a> (SEC). The SECU formed its mission to serve as a means to bolster collaborative academic endeavors of <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Conference#Member_universities" title="Southeastern Conference">SEC universities</a>. Its goals include highlighting the endeavors and achievements of SEC <a href="/wiki/Faculty_(academic_staff)" title="Faculty (academic staff)">faculty</a>, students and its universities and advancing the academic reputation of SEC universities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Kentucky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/University_of_Kentucky_student_life" title="University of Kentucky student life">University of Kentucky student life</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Students">Students</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Kentucky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Students">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The University of Kentucky strives for a diverse and international student population, with a selective admissions process.
</p><p>In fall 2014, there were 30,000 students enrolled for the first time. This is due in part by the high number of out-of-state students. The percentage mix of students at this time were 62% in state and 38% out-of-state. During this time, the freshman class was recorded at 5,000 students.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_government">Student government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Kentucky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Student government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The University of Kentucky Student Government Association (UKSGA) represents all undergraduate, graduate and professional students enrolled at the university in several critical ways. UKSGA exists to increase student influence over academic policy and to provide many helpful, creative and necessary student services. UKSGA also exists to protect and expand student substantive and procedural rights with the university and surrounding municipalities. Finally, UKSGA exists to better represent the student body in relations with faculty, administration, Board of Trustees and the Commonwealth of Kentucky.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup>
</p><p>UKSGA includes an Executive, Legislative, and Judicial Branch.
</p>
<ul><li>Executive Branch: oversees day-to-day operations, manages budget, and facilitates major programs.</li>
<li>Legislative Branch: includes the Student Senate. There are 46 legislators in this branch. Their goal is to allocate funds, approve presidential appointments, facilitate legislative changes, and represent the larger student voice.</li>
<li>Judicial: composed of one Chief Justice and six Supreme Court Justices. The Supreme Court rules on the constitutionality of legislation, handles claims levied against SGA officials, hears any election rules violation complaints and validates election results.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Several of their current programs include:
</p>
<ul><li>Legacy: a resource to help students create a lasting legacy on campus<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></li>
<li>Cat's Cruiser: a late night transportation service designed to enhance the safety efforts of the university and surrounding community in partnership with Lextran.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></li>
<li>Safe CATS: provides UK students with a safer way to travel around campus by having SafeCats team members escort students to their destinations on-foot or by golf cart<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></li>
<li>Student Legal Services: free on-site consultation for any legal issue by a local attorney<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></li>
<li>Tally Cats: an attendance-based incentive program for students that provides rewards for attending and participating in on-campus events.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></li>
<li>Wildcat Interest Group: a governmental relations division to promote civic engagement and lobby for University students locally and federally, including internship opportunities<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></li>
<li>Childcare Grants: available for part-time and full-time UK students, both at the undergraduate and graduate level, who need financial assistance for day-care service for their children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></li>
<li>Scholarships<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></li>
<li>Student Organization Funding: General Funding Grants, Club Sports Grants, Service Grants, and Senate Special Projects<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Several distinguished Student Body Presidents include Governor Steve Beshear.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_media">Student media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Kentucky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Student media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Electrical and Computer Engineering Department was the home of one of the earliest college amateur <a href="/wiki/Radio_station" title="Radio station">radio stations</a> in the United States, beginning with <a href="/wiki/W4JP" title="W4JP">W4JP</a> that began continuous operation prior to <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> In 1927, the station was relicensed as 9JL (later W9JL).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup>
</p><p>Students currently run two independent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frequency_Modulation" title="Frequency Modulation">FM</a> stations. The first, 91.3 FM <a href="/wiki/WUKY" title="WUKY">WUKY</a>, is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adult_Album_Alternative" title="Adult Album Alternative">Triple-A</a> station and was the first university-owned FM radio station in the United States and Kentucky's first public radio station.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WUKY_About_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-WUKY_About-67">[67]</a></sup> The operations started on October 17, 1940 as <a href="/wiki/WBKY" title="WBKY">WBKY</a> out of <a href="/wiki/Beattyville,_Kentucky" title="Beattyville, Kentucky">Beattyville</a>, although the station moved five years later to Lexington.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WUKY_About_67-1"><a href="#cite_note-WUKY_About-67">[67]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1971, WBKY was one of the first to carry NPR's "All Things Considered" and helped debut <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Public_Radio" title="National Public Radio">National Public Radio</a>, changing its call letters to WUKY in 1989 to better reflect its affiliation with the university. In 2007, it became the first Lexington radio station to broadcast in high-definition digital radio.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WUKY_About_67-2"><a href="#cite_note-WUKY_About-67">[67]</a></sup> The second is 88.1 FM <a href="/wiki/WRFL" title="WRFL">WRFL</a> which has been in operation since 1988.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WRFL_About_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-WRFL_About-68">[68]</a></sup> WRFL is operated by students and broadcasts live 24 hours a day, 7 days a week, and features music that is spread across most genres.
</p><p>The campus is also served by the <a href="/wiki/The_Kentucky_Kernel" title="The Kentucky Kernel">Kentucky Kernel</a>, a student-run, financially independent daily newspaper, with the first issue published in 1915.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> The official <a href="/wiki/Yearbook" title="Yearbook">yearbook</a> of the University of Kentucky is the <i>Kentuckian</i>, first published in 1906.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKChron_11-10"><a href="#cite_note-UKChron-11">[11]</a></sup> The <i>Kentuckian</i> was preceded by at least one previous book, the <i>Echo</i>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greek_life">Greek life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Kentucky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Greek life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Nineteen <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities" title="Fraternities and sororities">sororities</a> and twenty-three <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities" title="Fraternities and sororities">fraternities</a> serve the university, representing over 3,000 students with a budget of $3.2 million per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> The governing bodies include the <a href="/wiki/National_Pan-Hellenic_Council" title="National Pan-Hellenic Council">National Pan-Hellenic Council</a>, an organization for nine historically black organizations, international Greek assemblies, the <a href="/wiki/National_Panhellenic_Conference" title="National Panhellenic Conference">National Panhellenic Conference</a> for sororities and the <a href="/wiki/North-American_Interfraternity_Conference" title="North-American Interfraternity Conference">Interfraternity Council</a> for the fraternities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup>
There are many non-Greek organizations on campus, like <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Kappa_Psi" title="Alpha Kappa Psi">Alpha Kappa Psi</a>, an internationally recognized Professional Business Fraternity and <a href="/wiki/Tau_Beta_Sigma" title="Tau Beta Sigma">Tau Beta Sigma</a>, a band fraternity.  The university also hosts a chapter of the <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Phi_Omega" title="Alpha Phi Omega">Alpha Phi Omega</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Co-educational" title="Co-educational">co-educational</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Service_fraternity" title="Service fraternity">service fraternity</a>.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Kentucky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RupparenaK.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="290" data-file-width="412" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/RupparenaK.JPG/220px-RupparenaK.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/RupparenaK.JPG/330px-RupparenaK.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/08/RupparenaK.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RupparenaK.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Kentucky cheerleaders at <a href="/wiki/Rupp_Arena" title="Rupp Arena">Rupp Arena</a> performing the traditional "Big K" cheer during a basketball game. Seating Capacity of Rupp Arena is 23,500.</div></div></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kentucky_Wildcats" title="Kentucky Wildcats">Kentucky Wildcats</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Kentucky_Wildcats_men%27s_basketball" title="Kentucky Wildcats men's basketball">Kentucky Wildcats men's basketball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kentucky_Wildcats_football" title="Kentucky Wildcats football">Kentucky Wildcats football</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Kentucky_cheerleading_squad" title="University of Kentucky cheerleading squad">University of Kentucky cheerleading squad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kentucky_Wildcats_women%27s_basketball" title="Kentucky Wildcats women's basketball">Kentucky Wildcats women's basketball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kentucky_Wildcats_men%27s_soccer" title="Kentucky Wildcats men's soccer">Kentucky Wildcats men's soccer</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kentucky_Wildcats_softball" title="Kentucky Wildcats softball">Kentucky Wildcats softball</a></div>
<p>University of Kentucky student-athletes compete as the Wildcats under colors Kentucky blue and white.
</p><p>Beginning in the 1890s, students at the A&amp;M scheduled <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">football</a> games with neighboring colleges.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_HIS3_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-UK_HIS3-73">[73]</a></sup> In 1902, the <a href="/wiki/Kentucky_Wildcats_women%27s_basketball" title="Kentucky Wildcats women's basketball">women's basketball</a> program began on campus,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_HIS3_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-UK_HIS3-73">[73]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Kentucky_Wildcats_men%27s_basketball" title="Kentucky Wildcats men's basketball">men's team</a> was added one year later. The "<a href="/wiki/Wildcat" title="Wildcat">Wildcats</a>" became associated with the university shortly after a <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">football</a> victory over <a href="/wiki/Illinois_Fighting_Illini_football" title="Illinois Fighting Illini football">Illinois</a> on October 9, 1909.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_TRAD_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-UK_TRAD-5">[5]</a></sup> The then-chief of the military department, Commandant Carbuiser, stated that the team had "fought like wildcats." The slogan was later adopted by the university, and a costumed mascot debuted in 1976.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_TRAD_5-4"><a href="#cite_note-UK_TRAD-5">[5]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1930, then-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_school" title="High school">high school</a> coach <a href="/wiki/Adolph_Rupp" title="Adolph Rupp">Adolph Rupp</a> was hired as a basketball coach for the university. He had a career that would span 42 years until 1972.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKChron_11-11"><a href="#cite_note-UKChron-11">[11]</a></sup> During his tenure, he led the <a href="/wiki/Kentucky_Wildcats_men%27s_basketball" title="Kentucky Wildcats men's basketball">men's basketball team</a> to four <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> championships in 1948, 1949, 1951 and 1958.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_HIS3_73-2"><a href="#cite_note-UK_HIS3-73">[73]</a></sup> The Wildcats later won a fifth championship under <a href="/wiki/Joe_B._Hall" title="Joe B. Hall">Joe B. Hall</a> in 1978, another in 1996 under <a href="/wiki/Rick_Pitino" title="Rick Pitino">Rick Pitino</a> and the next under <a href="/wiki/Tubby_Smith" title="Tubby Smith">Orlando "Tubby" Smith</a> in 1998.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_HIS3_73-3"><a href="#cite_note-UK_HIS3-73">[73]</a></sup> In 2007, the University of Kentucky named <a href="/wiki/Billy_Gillispie" title="Billy Gillispie">Billy Gillispie</a> as the head coach of the men's basketball team and on March 30, 2009, the university named <a href="/wiki/John_Calipari" title="John Calipari">John Calipari</a> as the head coach of the Wildcats. Calipari coached the team to its eighth national title in 2012.
</p><p>On December 21, 2009, the men's basketball team reached another milestone, becoming the first college basketball team to reach 2000 all-time wins. The 2000th win was an 88–44 victory over the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Drexel_Dragons_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2009–10 Drexel Dragons men's basketball team">Drexel Dragons</a>. Kentucky was also the first school to reach the 1000 all-time wins, which they accomplished in 1969.
</p><p>The university boasts of numerous national championships, with its latest coming in 2012 when the men's basketball team won its eighth national title. UK also boasts of a <a href="/wiki/Cross_country_running" title="Cross country running">cross country</a> national team championship (women's, 1988), eight individual championships in <a href="/wiki/Artistic_gymnastics" title="Artistic gymnastics">gymnastics</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Summer_Olympic_Games" title="Summer Olympic Games">Olympic</a> medalist in <a href="/wiki/Track_and_field" title="Track and field">track and field</a>, and 21 national championships in <a href="/wiki/Cheerleading" title="Cheerleading">cheerleading</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_FACTS_26-5"><a href="#cite_note-UK_FACTS-26">[26]</a></sup> After defeating number-one ranked Oklahoma 13–7 in the Sugar Bowl under legendary coach Bear Bryant, Kentucky is also an NCAA-recognized co-national champion for the 1950 season.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:KentuckyCommonwealthStadium-EZInterior.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="685" data-file-width="1472" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/KentuckyCommonwealthStadium-EZInterior.jpg/275px-KentuckyCommonwealthStadium-EZInterior.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/KentuckyCommonwealthStadium-EZInterior.jpg/413px-KentuckyCommonwealthStadium-EZInterior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/KentuckyCommonwealthStadium-EZInterior.jpg/550px-KentuckyCommonwealthStadium-EZInterior.jpg 2x" width="275"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:KentuckyCommonwealthStadium-EZInterior.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Pregame of 2005 Kentucky vs. Auburn game.</div></div></div>
<p>The University of Kentucky Dance team is currently ranked 5th in the nation in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hip_Hop" title="Hip Hop">Hip Hop</a> and 7th in <a href="/wiki/Pom-pom" title="Pom-pom">Pom</a> at Universal Dance Association.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup>
</p><p>Other athletic programs sponsored at the varsity level include <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">baseball</a>, men's and women's <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, men's and women's <a href="/wiki/Cross_country_running" title="Cross country running">cross country running</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">football</a>, men's and women's <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a>, women's <a href="/wiki/Artistic_gymnastics" title="Artistic gymnastics">gymnastics</a>, the coeducational sport of <a href="/wiki/Shooting_sports" title="Shooting sports">rifle</a>, men's and women's <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">soccer</a>, women's <a href="/wiki/Softball" title="Softball">softball</a>, men's and women's <a href="/wiki/Swimming_(sport)" title="Swimming (sport)">swimming</a> and <a href="/wiki/Diving" title="Diving">diving</a>, men's and women's <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a>, men's and women's <a href="/wiki/Track_and_field" title="Track and field">track and field</a> and women's <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> The school also has a popular club-level men's <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a> team and a rugby program that competes at the Division 1 level.
</p><p>The University of Kentucky football coach is <a href="/wiki/Mark_Stoops" title="Mark Stoops">Mark Stoops</a>, named the successor to <a href="/wiki/Joker_Phillips" title="Joker Phillips">Joker Phillips</a>, who was the first African American football coach in Kentucky's history.
</p><p>Notable among a number of songs commonly played and sung at various events such as <a href="/wiki/Graduation" title="Graduation">commencement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Convocation" title="Convocation">convocation</a> and athletic games is the University of Kentucky <a href="/wiki/Fight_song" title="Fight song">fight song</a>: <i><a href="/wiki/On,_On,_U_of_K" title="On, On, U of K">On, On, U of K</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-songs_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-songs-76">[76]</a></sup> Additionally, the song <i>Kentucky Fight</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-songs_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-songs-76">[76]</a></sup> is played before games.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus">Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Kentucky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Campus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WilliamtyounglibraryUK.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="275" data-file-width="435" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/WilliamtyounglibraryUK.JPG/250px-WilliamtyounglibraryUK.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/WilliamtyounglibraryUK.JPG/375px-WilliamtyounglibraryUK.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6a/WilliamtyounglibraryUK.JPG 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WilliamtyounglibraryUK.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Completed in 1998, the William T. Young Library serves both the university campus and the Commonwealth of Kentucky</div></div></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Kentucky_buildings" title="List of University of Kentucky buildings">List of University of Kentucky buildings</a></div>
<p>The University of Kentucky offers seven main dining facilities, 23 residence halls, and numerous recreation facilities spread between three distinct campuses: north, south, and central. It is also home to more than 250 student-run organizations.
</p><p>The university campus is home to numerous notable structures, such as <a href="/wiki/Main_Building_(University_of_Kentucky)" title="Main Building (University of Kentucky)">Main Building</a>, a four-story administration building dating to 1882,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKChron_11-12"><a href="#cite_note-UKChron-11">[11]</a></sup> which was gutted by fire on May 15, 2001. The cause of the blaze was attributed to a welders torch during repairs to the building's roof. Total costs for reconstruction after the fire exceeded $17 million. The Patterson Office Tower is the tallest building on campus. The university is also home to several major construction projects, including the <a href="/wiki/Albert_B._Chandler_Hospital" title="Albert B. Chandler Hospital">Albert B. Chandler Hospital</a> expansion. As of 2016, construction projects include Student Center renovation and expansion, and Alumni Gym.
</p><p>The University of Kentucky once operated 14 <a href="/wiki/Community_college" title="Community college">community colleges</a> with more than 100 extended sites, centers and campuses under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Kentucky%27s_Community_College_System" title="University of Kentucky's Community College System">Kentucky Community and Technical College System</a>, but relinquished control under the <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Kentucky#Postsecondary_Education_Improvement_Act_of_1997" title="Education in Kentucky">Postsecondary Education Improvement Act of 1997</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DI_070103_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-DI_070103-77">[77]</a></sup> The network of community colleges is now known as the <a href="/wiki/Kentucky_Community_and_Technical_College_System" title="Kentucky Community and Technical College System">Kentucky Community and Technical College System</a> (KCTCS). Adjoining Lexington Community College, despite the reorganization of the community colleges, remained integrated with the university, but separated from the University of Kentucky in 2004 and became a part of KCTCS; it is now known as <a href="/wiki/Bluegrass_Community_and_Technical_College" title="Bluegrass Community and Technical College">Bluegrass Community and Technical College</a>.
</p><p>The College of Engineering currently operates a satellite campus in <a href="/wiki/Paducah,_Kentucky" title="Paducah, Kentucky">Paducah</a>, located on the campus of <a href="/wiki/West_Kentucky_Community_and_Technical_College" title="West Kentucky Community and Technical College">West Kentucky Community and Technical College</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WKCTCS_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-WKCTCS-78">[78]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Funkhouser_building.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2184" data-file-width="2912" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Funkhouser_building.jpg/250px-Funkhouser_building.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Funkhouser_building.jpg/375px-Funkhouser_building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Funkhouser_building.jpg/500px-Funkhouser_building.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Funkhouser_building.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Funkhouser Building</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus_libraries">Campus libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Kentucky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Campus libraries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The University of Kentucky is home to nine campus libraries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> Among them is the William T. Young Library, which houses houses a general undergraduate collection and social sciences, humanities, business, biology, and agricultural materials. The library is also a<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federal_Depository_Library" title="Federal Depository Library">Federal Depository Library</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Public_library" title="Public library">public library</a> for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Kentucky" title="Commonwealth of Kentucky">Commonwealth of Kentucky</a>. Libraries include:
</p>
<ul><li><a class="external text" href="http://libraries.uky.edu/AIC" rel="nofollow">Agricultural Information Center</a></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://libraries.uky.edu/Design" rel="nofollow">Design Library</a></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://libraries.uky.edu/Educ" rel="nofollow">Education Library</a></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://library.law.uky.edu/home" rel="nofollow">Law Library</a></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://libraries.uky.edu/FAlib" rel="nofollow">Lucille Caudill Little Fine Arts Library and Learning Center</a></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://libraries.uky.edu/MCL" rel="nofollow">Medical Center Library</a></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://libraries.uky.edu/SciEng" rel="nofollow">Science &amp; Engineering Library</a></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://libraries.uky.edu/SC" rel="nofollow">Special Collections Research Center</a></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://libraries.uky.edu/WTYL" rel="nofollow">William T. Young Library</a></li></ul>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Atrium_of_Don_and_Cathy_Jacobs_Science_Building.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4320" data-file-width="2432" height="391" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Atrium_of_Don_and_Cathy_Jacobs_Science_Building.jpg/220px-Atrium_of_Don_and_Cathy_Jacobs_Science_Building.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Atrium_of_Don_and_Cathy_Jacobs_Science_Building.jpg/330px-Atrium_of_Don_and_Cathy_Jacobs_Science_Building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Atrium_of_Don_and_Cathy_Jacobs_Science_Building.jpg/440px-Atrium_of_Don_and_Cathy_Jacobs_Science_Building.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Atrium_of_Don_and_Cathy_Jacobs_Science_Building.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Interior of new science building</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:University_of_Kentucky_Arboretum_-_DSC09377.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3240" data-file-width="4320" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/University_of_Kentucky_Arboretum_-_DSC09377.JPG/250px-University_of_Kentucky_Arboretum_-_DSC09377.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/University_of_Kentucky_Arboretum_-_DSC09377.JPG/375px-University_of_Kentucky_Arboretum_-_DSC09377.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/University_of_Kentucky_Arboretum_-_DSC09377.JPG/500px-University_of_Kentucky_Arboretum_-_DSC09377.JPG 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:University_of_Kentucky_Arboretum_-_DSC09377.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>UK Arboretum</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus_landmarks">Campus landmarks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Kentucky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Campus landmarks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The University of Kentucky has several noteworthy landmarks:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Kroger_Field" title="Kroger Field">Kroger Field</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Memorial_Coliseum_(Lexington)" title="Memorial Coliseum (Lexington)">Memorial Coliseum</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Memorial_Hall,_University_of_Kentucky" title="Memorial Hall, University of Kentucky">Memorial Hall</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Singletary_Center_for_the_Arts" title="Singletary Center for the Arts">Singletary Center for the Arts</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Kentucky_Art_Museum" title="University of Kentucky Art Museum">University of Kentucky Art Museum</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Kentucky/Lexington-Fayette_Urban_County_Government_Arboretum" title="University of Kentucky/Lexington-Fayette Urban County Government Arboretum">University of Kentucky/Lexington-Fayette Urban County Government Arboretum</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Kentucky_Research_and_Education_Center_Botanical_Garden" title="University of Kentucky Research and Education Center Botanical Garden">University of Kentucky Research and Education Center Botanical Garden</a></li>
<li>Wildcat Alumni Plaza</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/William_T._Young_Library" title="William T. Young Library">William T. Young Library</a></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_faculty">Notable faculty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Kentucky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Notable faculty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Arthur_G._Hunt" title="Arthur G. Hunt">Arthur G. Hunt</a>,  American plant and soils scientist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ronald_Werner-Wilson" title="Ronald Werner-Wilson">Ronald Werner-Wilson</a> (born 1972), Chair of the Family Studies Department and Kathryn Louise Chellgren Endowed Professor for Research in Family Studies</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kimberly_W._Anderson" title="Kimberly W. Anderson">Kimberly W. Anderson</a>, Chemist, Gill Eminent Professor of Chemical Engineering and Associate Dean for Administration and Academic Affairs in the College of Engineering</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_alumni">Notable alumni</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Kentucky&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Notable alumni">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Kentucky_alumni" title="List of University of Kentucky alumni">List of University of Kentucky alumni</a></div>
<p>The university has over 140,246 alumni in the state of Kentucky,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> 216,737 in the United States,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> and 1,119 internationally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> The University of Kentucky Alumni Association is the primary affiliation for former students and faculty, and is located at the corner of Rose Street and Euclid Avenue. The building, dedicated in 1963, is named for Helen G. King, the first permanent director of the association and was former "Miss University of Kentucky". The association also meets at <a href="/wiki/Spindletop_Hall" title="Spindletop Hall">Spindletop Hall</a>, a large mansion along Iron Works Pike, which serves as a central alumni gathering point.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup>
</p><p>The University of Kentucky boasts seven governors, including former <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Kentucky" title="Governor of Kentucky">Governor of Kentucky</a> <a href="/wiki/Steve_Beshear" title="Steve Beshear">Steve Beshear</a>, former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Governor_of_Ohio" title="Governor of Ohio">Governor of Ohio</a> <a href="/wiki/Ted_Strickland" title="Ted Strickland">Ted Strickland</a>, former <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_North_Carolina" title="Governor of North Carolina">Governor of North Carolina</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beverly_Perdue" title="Beverly Perdue">Beverly Perdue</a>, and former governors <a href="/wiki/Ernie_Fletcher" title="Ernie Fletcher">Ernie Fletcher</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_E._Patton" title="Paul E. Patton">Paul E. Patton</a> and Arkansas' <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tom_Jefferson_Terral" title="Tom Jefferson Terral">Tom Jefferson Terral</a>, and former governor, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Senator" title="U.S. Senator">U.S. Senator</a> and Commissioner of <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> <a href="/wiki/Happy_Chandler" title="Happy Chandler">Albert "Happy" Chandler</a>. It also claims <a href="/wiki/Ken_Lucas" title="Ken Lucas">Ken Lucas</a>, a former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._representative" title="U.S. representative">U.S. representative</a> from the commonwealth's fourth <a href="/wiki/Congressional_district" title="Congressional district">congressional district</a>, United Methodist Bishop <a href="/wiki/Alfred_W._Gwinn" title="Alfred W. Gwinn">Alfred W. Gwinn</a>, current <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Senator" title="U.S. Senator">U.S. Senator</a> <a href="/wiki/Mitch_McConnell" title="Mitch McConnell">Mitch McConnell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bill_Gatton" title="Bill Gatton">Carol Gatton</a>, an automobile dealer executive and donor of the largest gift ever to the university, and Paul Chellgren, <a href="/wiki/Chairman" title="Chairman">Chairman</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CEO" title="CEO">CEO</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ashland_Inc." title="Ashland Inc.">Ashland Inc.</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> The university was also the home of Dr. <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Hunt_Morgan" title="Thomas Hunt Morgan">Thomas Hunt Morgan</a>, a scientist and winner of the 1933 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physiology_or_Medicine" title="Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine">Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/William_Lipscomb" title="William Lipscomb">William Lipscomb</a>, 1976 winner of the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Chemistry" title="Nobel Prize in Chemistry">Nobel Prize in Chemistry</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKChron_11-13"><a href="#cite_note-UKChron-11">[11]</a></sup> The university claims actors such as <a href="/wiki/Ashley_Judd" title="Ashley Judd">Ashley Judd</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup>
</p>
<center>
